Proof of God's Power Over All Possibles
Imam Razi proves God's power over all possible things by the commonality of possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's proof that God is powerful over all possible things and that no possible exists except by His power.

Core Idea
Possibility (imkaan) is the common basis for God's power over all possible things.

This passage from Imam Razi's Muhassal presents a unique argument for the universality of God's power. Starting from the Ash'ari position, Razi establishes that the attribute that makes a thing an object of divine power is its possibility (imkaan). Because all possible things share this attribute, God's power must extend to all, and no other agent can independently bring about any possible thing. We'll walk through this argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then refer to the literal translation. Pay attention to the flow of the argument.
The argument is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the basis for being an object of power
Locate where Razi states what makes a thing a valid object of God's power. Note that it is possibility (imkaan), not necessity or impossibility.
3
Understand the argument from commonality
Notice that possibility is a shared description among all possible things. Razi argues that without a particularizer, God's power must apply to all possibles.
This step establishes the universality of God's power.
4
Grasp the elimination of other agents
Razi then considers the scenario of another independent agent. Follow his three-part analysis showing that any co-existence leads to impossibility.
This confirms that no possible can exist except by God's power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الممكنات
( مسألة : مذهب أصحابنا أن الله تعالى قادر على كل المقدورات خلافا لجميع الفرق )
انا أن ما لاجله صح فى البعض أن يكون مقدور الله تعالى هو الإمكان ، لأن ما عداه إما الوجوب وإما الامتناع وهما يحيلان المقدورية لكن الإمكان وصف مشترك فيه بين الممكنات فيكون الكل مشتركا في صحة مقدورية الله تعالى ، فلو اختصت قادريته بالبعض افتقر إلى المخصص، وإذا ثبت أنه قادر على جميع وجب أن لا يوجد شيء من الممكنات إلا بقدرته إذ لو فرضنا شيئا آخر مؤثرا لكانا إذا اجتمعا على ذلك الممكن فإما أن يقمع ذلك الممكن بهما فيجتمع على الأثر الواحد مؤثران مستقلان وهو محال أو لا يقع بواحد منهما وهو محال لأن المانع من وقوعه بهذا وقوعه بذاك فمالم يوجد وقوعه بهذا لا يمتنع وقوعه بذاك، فلو امتنع وقوعه بهذا أو ذاك لزم وقوعه بهذا وذاك حتى يكون وقوعه بكل واحد منهما مانعا بالآخر وذلك محال ، وإما أن يقع بأحدهما دون الآخر وهو محال لأن كل واحد لما كان مستقلا بالتأثير كان وقوعه بأحدهما دون الآخر ترجيحا لأحد طرق الممكن على الآخر بلا مرجح وهو محال ، فثبت أن الممكنات واقع بقدرة الله تعالى وتعلقاته
Possible things. (Question: The doctrine of our companions is that God Almighty is powerful over all possible things, contrary to all sects.) [I say] that that because of which some [things] are correct to be objects of God's power is possibility (al-imkaan), because what is other than it is either necessity or impossibility, and both prevent being an object of power. But possibility is a description shared among all possible things, so all share in the correctness of being objects of God's power. Thus if His power were restricted to some [things], it would need a particularizer. And when it is established that He is powerful over all, it necessarily follows that nothing among possible things exists except by His power. For if we suppose another agent, then when they both act upon that possible, either that possible occurs by both of them, so two independent agents would meet upon one effect, which is impossible; or it occurs by neither of them, which is impossible because the prevention of its occurrence by one is its occurrence by the other, and as long as its occurrence by this one does not occur, its occurrence by that one is not prevented. So if its occurrence by this one or that one were prevented, it would necessitate its occurrence by this one and that one, so that its occurrence by each one would prevent the other, and that is impossible. Or it occurs by one of them without the other, which is impossible because each one, since it is independent in causing, its occurrence by one without the other would be a preference of one way of the possible over another without a preferrer, which is impossible. Thus it is established that possible things exist by the power of God Almighty and His attachments.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God is powerful over all possible things and that no possible exists except by His power. Imam Razi first states the Ash'ari position: God is powerful over all that is possible (maqduurat). He then gives the basis: the attribute that makes a thing a valid object of divine power is possibility (imkaan). Necessity and impossibility both preclude being an object of power. Since possibility is a common description among all possible things, they all equally can be objects of God's power. If God's power were restricted to some, there would need to be a particularizer (mukhassis) to specify the scope, which is arbitrary. Therefore, God is powerful over all possible things. Then Razi argues that if God is powerful over all possibles, no possible can exist except by His power. He considers the scenario of another agent alongside God. He examines three possibilities: (1) the effect occurs by both agents together — two independent agents acting on one effect is impossible (impossible because the effect would have two sufficient causes independently). (2) The effect occurs by neither — this leads to contradiction because if one agent prevents the other, then as long as the effect does not occur by one, its occurrence by the other is not prevented. If it were prevented by both, then it would have to occur by both to prevent each other, which is circular. (3) The effect occurs by one of them alone — this is a preference without a preferrer, also impossible. Hence, no other agent can be independent; all possible existence is by God's power.

Key Terms
قادر
مقدورات
الإمكان
الوجوب
الامتناع
مخصص
مؤثر
ترجيح بلا مرجح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that possibility (imkaan) alone is not sufficient to prove that God's power extends to all possibles, or that some possibles might be outside His power due to some other attribute.
Correction: Razi shows that the only relevant attribute for being an object of power is possibility. Necessity and impossibility exclude something from being a possible object, but possibility is a common description. Without a particularizer, the commonality forces universality.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Razi, what is the basis for something being an object of God's power?
A) Its existence in the world
B) Its possibility (imkaan)
C) Its need for a creator
D) Its being a substance

Key Takeaway
God's power extends to all possible things because they share the attribute of possibility, and no possible thing exists except by His power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that nothing in your life happens except by God's power? Think of a recent success or failure. Did you attribute it to your own ability or to God? If you truly believed that no other agent has independent power, would your gratitude and reliance be different? Commit to saying 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' before starting any task today to remind yourself of this truth.
?
When you face hardship, do you sometimes feel that your own efforts are futile? But if God's power is over all possibles, then your efforts are still by His power. How does that change your view of your own agency? Write down one area where you need to acknowledge God's exclusive power more.
?
Are there any 'secondary causes' in your life that you treat as independent? Your job, your health, your relationships? Razi's proof shows that no other agent can independently cause. Does your heart really believe that? What would change if you lived that conviction today?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
6 min
Critique of Razi's Proof for God's Exclusive Agency
The commentator criticizes Imam Razi's argument that no possible exists except by God's power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the commentator argues that being powerful over all possibles does not make God the exclusive actual agent, and the distinction between capability (qudra) and causation (ta'thir).

Core Idea
Power alone does not cause; will is the key to actual agency.

The commentator now scrutinizes Imam Razi's proof that God is the sole agent. He points out a logical gap: power without will does not necessitate causation. Moreover, both God and servants can be capable of the same act, but only one wills it. This lesson unpacks this subtle distinction and its implications for divine and human action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the full translation. Notice the commentator's critical tone and the key terms.
The passage is dense; reading twice is helpful.
2
Identify the distinction between qaadir and mu'aththir
Find where the commentator distinguishes between 'powerful over' (qaadir) and 'agent' (mu'aththir). Understand that the first does not automatically imply the second.
This is the core logical point.
3
Understand the role of will in causation
Note that the commentator says power alone is insufficient; will (iraada) is required for an effect. This explains why God is not the agent of everything He is capable of.
4
Grasp the Ahl al-Sunna position on two capable beings
The commentator states that both God and the servant can be capable (qaadiraan) of one thing, but the actual agent is only one of them. This contradicts Razi's implication that two capable beings cannot coexist for one act.
This defends human capability without shirk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفى قوله إذا ثبت أنه قادر على جميع الممكنات وجب أن لا يوجد شيء من الممكنات إلا بقدرته ففيه نظر لأنه لا يلزم من كونه قادرا على جميع الممكنات كونه مؤثرا فى جميعها وإلا لزم منه وجود جميع الممكنات وذلك أن القدرة وحدها لا تكفى فى وجود التأثير بل يحتاج معها إلى الإرادة، والدليل الذي ذكره يدل على امتناع اجتماع مؤثرين على أثر واحد ولم أيدل على امتناع اجتماع قادرين على مقدور واحد ، بل الصحيح عند أهل السنة أن الله تعالى قادر على كل الممكنات وغير مؤثر فى كلها والعبد قادر على البعض وغير مؤثر ، فهما إذا قادران على شيء واحد ، أن المؤثر فيه أحدهما دون الآخر ، وإنما كان ذلك كذلك لكون المؤثر محتا جامع القدرة مع إلى الإرادة والقادر هو الذى له القدرة فقط من حيث هو قادر ، وعلى هذا التقدير لا يمتنع أن يكون في ممكن مؤثر غير الله تعالى إلا أن بعض ذلك بغير ماذكره وفى عبارته عند قوله أو يقع بواحد منهما وهو محال لأن المانع من وقوعه بذاك فمالم يوجد وقوعه بهذا لا يمتنع وقوعه بذاك ، موضع نظر إذ كان من الواجب أن يقول فمالم يوجد وقوعه بهذا وجب وقوعه بذاك إذ ذلك مؤثر خال عن الموانع ، وباقى الكلام هكذا فلو لم يقع بهذا وذلك وقع بذلك وبهذا وهو محال .
And in his statement: 'When it is established that He is powerful over all possible things, it necessarily follows that nothing among possible things exists except by His power' - there is a point of consideration. For it does not follow from His being powerful over all possible things that He is an agent (mu'aththir) in all of them; otherwise it would necessitate the existence of all possible things. That is because power alone is not sufficient for bringing about the effect; rather, will (iraada) is needed along with it. And the proof he mentioned indicates the impossibility of two agents (mu'aththirayn) meeting upon one effect, but it does not indicate the impossibility of two capable beings (qaadirayn) meeting upon one object of power (maqdoor). Rather, the correct position according to the Ahl al-Sunna is that God Almighty is powerful over all possible things but is not an agent in all of them, and the servant is powerful over some but is not an agent. So both are capable (qaadiraan) of one thing, but the agent in it is one of them. And that is so because the agent is one who combines power with will, while the capable (al-qaadir) is one who has power only, insofar as he is capable. On this basis, there is no impossibility that there be in a possible an agent other than God, except that some of that is not as he mentioned. And in his expression when he said 'or it occurs by one of them, which is impossible' because the preventer of its occurrence by this is its occurrence by that, and as long as its occurrence by this does not exist, its occurrence by that is not prevented - this is a point of consideration. For it was necessary to say: 'As long as its occurrence by this does not exist, its occurrence by that becomes necessary, since that is an agent free of obstacles.' And the rest of the speech similarly: 'And if it does not occur by this and that, then it occurs by that and this, which is impossible.'
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a commentator's critique of Imam Razi's proof in the previous lesson. The commentator points out an error: Razi argues that if God is powerful over all possibles, then no possible can exist except by His power, implying that God is the sole agent. The commentator says this does not follow, because power alone does not entail causation; will is also necessary. Therefore, God can be capable of many things without actually causing them (if He does not will them). Moreover, Razi's proof only addresses the impossibility of two independent agents (mu'aththirayn) acting on one effect, but it does not address the possibility of two capable beings (qaadirayn) being able to do the same thing. According to Ahl al-Sunna, both God and a servant can be capable of the same act, but only one actually does it. The agent is the one who both has power and wills. So Razi's argument overreaches. The commentator also criticizes the logical structure of Razi's proof, noting that if the occurrence by one agent is prevented by the other, then the absence of occurrence by one should entail occurrence by the other, not the paradox Razi describes. Thus, the proof as stated is flawed.

Key Terms
قادر
مؤثر
إرادة
قادران
مقدور واحد
أهل السنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God is powerful over everything, then everything that happens must be directly caused by God, and humans have no real part in action.
Correction: Power alone does not make one an agent; will is required. According to Ahl al-Sunna, both God and humans can be capable of the same act, but only one (the one who wills) is the actual agent. Thus, humans can be real agents without contradicting divine power.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what does the Ahl al-Sunna say about the relationship between God's power and the servant's power?
A) They cannot be capable of the same act.
B) Both can be capable of the same act, but only one is the actual agent.
C) The servant has no real power.
D) God's power is exclusive to all acts.

Key Takeaway
Power alone does not entail agency; will is necessary, and both God and humans can be capable of the same act without contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever attribute your successes to your own power alone, forgetting that without God's will your efforts yield nothing? How will you remind yourself that your power is merely capacity, not causation?
?
The passage shows that both God and the servant can be capable of the same act. How does this affect your view of your own actions and your dependence on God's will? Will you consciously surrender the actual agency to Allah in your daily deeds?
?
Razi's argument mistakenly thought power necessitates action. Where in your life do you assume that because you have ability, you are the one who brings about results? What specific step will you take today to rely on Allah's will rather than your own strength?
